- Tested on: vSRX V3 22.4R1, vSRX V2 22.4R1

- Access level: Full admin access/RCE
- Requirements: Access to the web interface, Works on default configurations
- Exploitation steps: 2
- Upload stager
- Execute stager
- Shodan query:
- Link: https://www.shodan.io/search?query=html%3A%22Juniper+Web+Device+Manager%22

## Target OS (specify builds, versions, 32/64 bits)

- Juniper JunOS versions 12.1 to 23.1R1 (2023 release)

## Vulnerable software (specify builds, versions, 32/64 bits)

- Juniper JunOS versions 12.1 to 23.1R1 (SRX firewalls all models/Builds)

## Vulnerability type or CVSS (memory corruption bug, logic bug, command injection bug, etc)

- Logic bug, Command injection.

## What are minimum privileges required to launch the exploit?

- None.

## What are privileges gained after successful exploitation?

- root level privileges on JunOS.

## Are additional credentials or authentication required?

- No

## What is an attack vector (zero-click, via document, via email, from intranet, etc)?

- zero-click.

## What is the number of vulnerabilities used in the exploit / exploit chain?

- 4

- No.

- No.

- 5-10 seconds.

## What is reliability of the exploit (in %)?

- 100%

## Is any interaction with vulnerable software required from the target user during exploitation?

- No.

## Is multi-versioning supported (capability of the exploit to perform on different versions of vulnerable software, determining the version automatically)?

- Yes.

## Is the exploit working on targer OS and software with default settings? If no, what settings and prerequisites (including packages, in case of Linux) should be met for successful exploitation?

- Yes.

## Is shellcode implemented in the exploit?

- No.

## How the payload is implemented?

- Not much, Light code editing in the PoC code or sepcify a file containing a payload (shell script).
